                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) DOS files of NVPOF, NVPOF-C, NVPOF-CC, NVPOF-CCN, and NVPOF-HE as indicated. The positive and negative values of DOS for the channels of spin up and down, respectively. b) The schematic structure of the NVPOF framework is marked by the selected migration path. c) Schematic illustration for migration pathway of Na<sup>+</sup> in the NVPOF-HE. d) Typical Na<sup>+</sup>-diffusion energy barriers of NVPOF-HE; specific Na<sup>+</sup>-diffusion energy barriers of e) NVPOF, f) NVPOF-C, g) NVPOF-CC, and h) NVPOF-CCN as indicated.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202403282-sec-0050-title">2.3 Electrochemical Evaluation of HC//NVPOF-HE Full Cells</h3>
            
            <p>To further evaluate the feasibility of our optimized NVPOF-HE as a cathode material for SIBs, we used the commercial HC as an anode material (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting Information) to assemble HC//NVPOF-HE full SIBs toward device-level electrochemical evaluation, as schematically in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403282-fig-0007">7a</a>. The HC anode delivers a discharge specific capacity of 226.8 and 121.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, along with a high columbic efficiency of ≈98.5% and ≈99.9% at 1 and 10 C, respectively. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403282-fig-0007">7b</a> displays the rate properties of the constructed cells within the voltage range from 2.3–4.4&nbsp;V. The full battery obtains a high average discharge capacity of 122.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 C (1 C = 130&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> based on the cathode), and even can maintain the reversible capacities as large as 96.5 and 51.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with the C rates up to 5 and 50 C, respectively, which corresponds to a capacity decay of 57.9% with a 250-fold increase in C rates. Moreover, the voltage platform interval of the full battery expands relatively with increasing current rates and maintains a relatively high operating voltage, as evidenced in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403282-fig-0007">7c</a>. The NVPOF-HE full battery can provide an amazing energy density of 463&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 C. It is worth noting that even when the rate is increased to 50 C, the material-level energy density can still reach 169&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>. Note that the achieved energy density of assembled device is compared with and/or better than other reported cells before (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). Besides this, the device provides an excellent reversible capacity of 115.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention rate of ≈97.5% and a Coulombic efficiency (CE) of over 99.4% after 200 consecutive cycles at 0.5 C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403282-fig-0007">7d</a>). More competitively, our assembled HC//NVPOF-HE device, as profiled in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403282-fig-0007">7e</a>, still renders a discharge capacity of 95.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, which is ≈93.8% of the initial capacity (≈101.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>), corresponding to 0.006% capacity attenuation per cycle, after 1000 uninterrupted cycles at 5 C rate. Furthermore, throughout these cycles, the CE approaches ≈100%, indicating the superb electrochemical stability and reversibility of our fabricated device. This undoubtedly demonstrates the excellent long-life cycling stability of our built commercializable HC//NVPOF-HE SIBs, which is compared to those of previously reported SIBs (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). For a more comprehensive assessment of the applicability of out SIBs, cycling performance was investigated at 50 and −20&nbsp;°C with a current rate of 1 C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a>, Supporting Information). Remarkably, the capacity retention of the full battery after 100 cycles can reach 94.7% (111.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, 50&nbsp;°C) and 98.2% (78.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, −20&nbsp;°C), along with the high CE values over cycling, demonstrating its superb wide-operating-temperature-range adaptability.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403282-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/a4cc850b-ea6a-4d88-8ba4-6789cbe45e3d/aenm202403282-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/a4cc850b-ea6a-4d88-8ba4-6789cbe45e3d/aenm202403282-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1b30501b-5aea-4b77-b8dd-7a049a9b4ebb/aenm202403282-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/a4cc850b-ea6a-4d88-8ba4-6789cbe45e3d/aenm202403282-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403282-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403282" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical evaluation of the HC//NVPOF SIBs: a) schematic illustration for the full cells; b) rate behaviors; c) charge/discharge profiles at C rates ranging from 0.2 to 50 C; long-cycle stability along with the CE data at d) 0.5 C and e) 5 C.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0060">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403282-sec-0060-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, in the work, the synergistic design (i.e., tiny HE doping and nano-engineering) was smartly proposed to finely fabricate nano-dimensional NVPOF-HE as the competitive cathode materials toward high-performance SIBs. With the collaborative contributions from polyvinyl pyrrolidone and tiny HE doping, the grain refinement effect occurred in the formation of nano-phase NVPOF-HE. The comprehensive theoretical simulation/calculations and physicochemical characterizations solidly highlighted the significant role of tiny HE doping in promoting ion/charge diffusion kinetics, high-voltage-range capacity contribution, and structural stability, which rationally accounted for the competitive sodium-storage properties of nano NVPOF-HE cathode. Accordingly, the NVPOF-HE delivered a larger specific capacity of ≈73.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 50 C rate, and a modest capacity degradation of ≈0.0002% per cycle after 4000 consecutive charge–discharge cycles at 10 C, which are hugely superior to single-ion/dual-ion/triple-ion doped nano-counterparts, and other reported state-of-the-art NVPOF cathodes. More encouragingly, the constructed NVPOF-HE//HC SIBs obtained a high materials-level capacity of 51.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and energy density of 169&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 50 C rate, along with a remarkable electrochemical stability (≈93.8% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 5 C). More meaningfully, our findings and in-depth understandings achieved here will provide invaluable guidance for developing other advanced cathode materials toward high-energy-density SIBs with high rates and longevity, and even other rechargeable batteries.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403282-sec-0070-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0080">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0090">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202403282-sec-0100-title"> Synthesis of a Series of NVPOF-Based Samples</h4>
                  
                  <p>The nano NVPOF-HE was synthesized by the method described as follows. Typically, 2&nbsp;g of polyvinyl pyrrolidone (PVP, molecular weight 1&nbsp;300&nbsp;000) was added to the mixed solution of 10&nbsp;mL of de-ionized water (DIW) and 10&nbsp;mL of anhydrous ethanol (AE), and violently stirred until completely dissolved, which was marked as the solution A. Then, 1.94&nbsp;mmol of V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>, 6&nbsp;mmol of H<sub>2</sub>C<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O, and 0.024&nbsp;mmol of (Cr(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·9H<sub>2</sub>O, Mn(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·4H<sub>2</sub>O, Co(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O, Ni(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O, and Cu(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·3H<sub>2</sub>O) were added in 40&nbsp;mL of mixed solvent composed of DIW and AE at a volumetric ratio of 1:1 under constantly stirring for 30&nbsp;min at 70&nbsp;°C, and then, 4&nbsp;mmol of NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> and 6&nbsp;mmol of NaF were added in this mixed solution for another 30&nbsp;min to form the solution B. Afterward, the solution A was added into the solution B, and the resulting mixture was stirred in a water bath at 70&nbsp;°C for 30&nbsp;min. The homogenized solution was then transferred to a Teflon reactor (100&nbsp;mL) and held at 140&nbsp;°C for 24&nbsp;h. After cooling to room temperature, the supernatant was poured away, and the resulting precipitation was alternately centrifuged with DIW and AE. Thus, the centrifuged precipitation was dried overnight in a vacuum electric oven at 60&nbsp;°C. Finally, the NVPOF-HE was obtained by annealing the dried product at 500&nbsp;°C for 1&nbsp;h in an Argon atmosphere at a heating rate of 5&nbsp;°C per min.</p>
                  
                  <p>As for other ions-doped samples including Cr<sup>6+</sup> doped NVPOF (NVPOF-C), Cr<sup>6+</sup> and Co<sup>2+</sup> co-doped NVPOF (NVPOF-CC) and Cr<sup>6+</sup>, Co<sup>2+</sup>, and Ni<sup>2+</sup> co-doped NVPOF (NVPOF-CCN), the synthesis parameters were basically kept the same as those of NVPOF-HE just with the different doped ions. As for the phase-pure nano NVPOF, only 2&nbsp;mmol of V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> was added to provide transition metal atoms. For comparison, the micro-sized NVPOF was fabricated by using the same parameters with those of nano NVPOF just without the addition of PVP.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202403282-sec-0110-title"> Materials Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The crystalline structure characterizations were carried out by X-ray diffraction (XRD) by Rigaku Ultima IV (<i>Cu</i> K<i>α</i> radiation, <i>λ</i> = 1.5046 Å, 40&nbsp;kV, 120&nbsp;mA, Japan) at 1° per min over the 2<i>θ</i> range of 10–110 °. Rietveld refinement of XRD data was calculated by the GSAS/EXPGUI software. Morphologies and microstructures were studied by field-emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM, JEOL-6300F, 15&nbsp;kV), transmission electron microscopy (TEM), scanning TEM, and high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) (JEOL JEM-2100, operating at 200 KV) coupled with energy dispersive X-ray (EDX) analysis. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) measurements for evaluation of elemental species and chemical states were conducted by Thermo ESCALAB 250Xi using 284.8&nbsp;eV (C 1s) energy calibration. Thermal gravimetric analysis (TGA) of samples was conducted by thermal analyzer (DTG-60H) in air at a heating rate of 10&nbsp;°C min<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202403282-sec-0120-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The cathode electrodes were prepared by adding the active materials, carboxymethylcellulose (CMC) binder, and carbon black in de-ionized water (DIW) at a mass ratio of 8:1:1 and coating it on Al foil, and then dried in vacuum oven at 60&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h. The mass loading of electroactive materials was ≈1.6–2.2&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. For both half and full cells, the employed electrolyte and separator were 1.0&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> in a solvent of diglyme, and glass fiber membrane (GF/D), respectively. As for the HC anode, the slurry consisted of HC (BTR New Material Group Co., Ltd), carbon black, and carboxymethylcellulose sodium (8:1:1 in weight) was mixed well in NMP, and further coated on the Al foil. Note that for full devices, the capacity of cathode and anode electrodes was matched to be ≈1:1.1–1.2. Prior to the fabrication of HC//NVPOP-HE full SIBs, the pre-sodiation for the HC anodes was performed by making it closely contact sodium sheet for 12&nbsp;h in an Ar-filled glove box. All the cells were assembled and sealed in an Ar-filled glove box (MBRAUN UNIlab Plus, the contents of O<sub>2</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>O less than 0.1&nbsp;ppm).</p>
                  
                  <p>Typical charge–discharge and galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) tests were conducted on the Land test system (CT2001A, Wuhan China). Electrochemical evaluation at different temperatures was carried out on a temperature-controlled test chamber (Dongguan Kingjio TT5166 Temp and humid control equipment Co., Ltd., China). Cyclic voltammetry (CV) and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) were both performed on an IVIUM electrochemical workstation (The Netherlands). The EIS tests were measured at 4.5&nbsp;V from 0.01 to 10<sup>5</sup>&nbsp;Hz with an AC signal amplitude of 10&nbsp;mV.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403282-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202403282-sec-0130-title"> Calculation Detail</h4>
                  
                  <p>First-principles calculations were carried out using density functional theory (DFT) with generalized gradient approximation (GGA) of Perdew–Burke–Ernzerhof (PBE) implemented in the Vienna Ab-Initio Simulation Package (VASP).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403282-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403282-bib-0058_R_d39507008e2008" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Phys. Rev. B">58</a>, <a href="#aenm202403282-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403282-bib-0059_R_d39507008e2008" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - Mater. Sci. Eng. R">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The valence electronic states were expanded on the basis of plane waves with the core-valence interaction represented using the projector augmented plane wave (PAW) approach and a cutoff of 400&nbsp;eV.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403282-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403282-bib-0055_R_d39507008e2013" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - ACS Nano">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Brillouin zone integration was sampled with 1×1×2 k-point meshes for geometry optimization. To deal with the low concentration of different dopants it was considered to be a rather large supercell containing 288 atoms as the structural model. The structures were fully relaxed until the maximum force on each atom becomes &lt;0.02&nbsp;eV&nbsp;Å<sup>−1</sup>. The climbing image nudged elastic band (CI-NEB) algorithm was employed to identify the transition state structures for Na migrations.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403282-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403282-bib-0056_R_d39507008e2021" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Phys. Rev. B">56</a>, <a href="#aenm202403282-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403282-bib-0057_R_d39507008e2021" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - J. Mater. Chem. A">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To handle the strong correlation of d electrons in transition metal atoms (V/Cr/Co/Ni/Mn/Cu), the DFT+U correction with U = 4&nbsp;eV was introduced in the calculation of electronic properties.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403282-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403282-bib-0060_R_d39507008e2026" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Phys. Rev. B">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
